msg:I stayed at this hotel with my partners from 2009 to 2019, but when the pandemic hit, we stopped coming to China for three years. This time, I decided to come with my family, and here's what we experienced:

Terrible service: they provided the cheapest baby crib and the cheapest bedding. There's not even a children's play area, and the breakfasts have become just awful compared to what they used to be. I gave them children's pasta to cook, and they just poured boiling water over it and served it. It was horrible. We left a valuable children's plate at breakfast and when we came back the next day, it was gone, and they said they didn't have it, which means they either threw it away or stole it.
The waiters barely understand English, and only after someone senior came over were we able to explain what we needed. We were constantly stressed and decided to change hotels to one with excellent service, and I am writing this review from such a place, where the service, crib, and food are top-notch.

But the most terrible moment came at the end when we were checking out. I simply asked for help as a tourist with calling a taxi through an app, as I had a lot of luggage and wanted to order a minivan, but I didn't have any money on my WeChat. I offered to give them 100 yuan in cash if they could help call a taxi. The chief manager approached and rudely and arrogantly stated that such a service does not fall within our hotel's policy, refusing us even though we were standing there with a child in our arms asking for help.

I was appalled by his behavior and stated that this was a terrible hotel that had gone downhill, and I asked for a complaint book to write all this down, although initially, I just wanted to leave and forget everything. But in response to my request for a complaint book, he handed me a piece of paper 5 by 5 cm in size and said, "Here, write on this." When I asked what this was, he replied, "Write your complaint here," and when I asked him to provide a real complaint book, he answered that the hotel does not have one. When I asked to call the manager, he said he was the manager.

I was shocked at how arrogantly and rudely he treated the customers. I have stayed at Hyatt hotels all over the world - in China, Indonesia, Europe, Japan, Russia, but I have never encountered such service anywhere.

name:L‚Äçe‚Äçi‚Äçc‚Äçe‚Äçs‚Äçt‚Äçe‚Äçr‚Äç ‚ÄçM‚Äça‚Äçn
info:Grand Park View King Room
info:Stayed in September 2021
info:Solo travelers
info:56 Reviews
rating:1.5
posted:Posted November 2, 2021
msg:I would only outline three problems, although there were, in fact, many more. The first is about room hygiene, which is supposed to be one of the most critical priorities for any hotel. Basically, what happened was that I discovered there were two pieces of used notepad papers right on top of the wash pan. The very existence of these papers could not have been more obvious. I did not find them particularly troubling at first, but I soon realized the severity of this problem. It was not these papers in themselves being the problem; the scary thing is the problem behind their very existence: given that the housekeeping could not even spot these two pieces of trash that I could immediately spot once I stepped into the room, how could I believe that they had done their job to have thoroughly cleaned the room? Given that they could not even clean these two simple papers, how can I believe they had done their jobs cleaning the bath, the shower, the desk, or even the bed? I understand that there was also a chance that the housekeeping had done everything but just accidentally omitted the two pieces of paper trash. I also recognize how busy the housekeeping team was, and I was and am very grateful for their services. However, the very existence of these two pieces of trash is still quite a blow to one‚Äôs confidence in the overall hygiene of the hotel.

The second problem is a typical one among the Hyatt properties I have visited ‚Äì they did not care about guests' room preferences, even if I had already notified them one day in advance. I asked my travel agency to inform the hotel about my room preferences one day before my arrival. The hotel confirmed they had taken note of that and would try to accommodate. However, the hotel not only did not make any arrangement in advance (which I will explain later how I discovered they did not), they did not even make that arrangement on the spot. How did I know they did not make the arrangement even on the spot? In the middle of the check-in process, suddenly recalling how irresponsive Hyatt hotels had been to my pre-arrival notes, I asked the lady helping me to check in whether she had seen my room preferences. Only on that spot did they browse through the system to check my preference. In other words, had I not reminded my preferences to the hotel again during check-in, the hotel would not have paid any attention to them. How can I be convinced that the hotel did spend even a little effort to accommodate my preferences, given that the check-in desk did not even know my preferences? There is only one possibility ‚Äì the reservation department had already helped me reserve a room in advance that matches my preferences. However, I could quickly rule out this possibility because the check-in desk told me, ‚ÄúOkay, we will try to find a room that best matches your preferences among all rooms that we have now". This reveals that not even the reservation department made the arrangement; otherwise, the check-in desk would not need to make the arrangement right on the spot. Overall, I find it highly believable that Grand Hyatt initially intended to totally ignore guests' room preference, given that the reservation team did not make the arrangement nor the check-in desk have done so had I had reminded them again. I do not find a hotel that would systematically neglect guests' preferences a decent hotel. Fortunately, the lady heading the front desk could fix the problems by arranging a room I preferred at last. However, the overall experience of realizing that the hotel did not intend to acknowledge guests' preferences without the guests' continuously reminding them is bothering.
----------------------------------------
